<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culinary_uses">Culinary uses</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:R%C3%A9duction_du_vin_rouge.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="426" data-file-width="640" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/R%C3%A9duction_du_vin_rouge.jpg/220px-R%C3%A9duction_du_vin_rouge.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/R%C3%A9duction_du_vin_rouge.jpg/330px-R%C3%A9duction_du_vin_rouge.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/R%C3%A9duction_du_vin_rouge.jpg/440px-R%C3%A9duction_du_vin_rouge.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:R%C3%A9duction_du_vin_rouge.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Reduction_(cooking)" title="Reduction (cooking)">Reduction</a> of red wine for a sauce by cooking it on a stovetop. It is called a reduction because the heat boils off some of the water, leaving a more concentrated, wine-flavoured sauce.</div></div></div>
<p>Wine is a popular and important <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Beverage" title="Beverage">beverage</a> that accompanies and enhances a wide range of cuisines, from the simple and traditional <a href="/wiki/Stew" title="Stew">stews</a> to the most sophisticated and complex <a href="/wiki/Haute_cuisine" title="Haute cuisine">haute cuisines</a>. Wine is often served with dinner. Sweet <a href="/wiki/Dessert_wine" title="Dessert wine">dessert wines</a> may be served with the <a href="/wiki/Dessert" title="Dessert">dessert</a> course. In fine restaurants in Western countries, wine typically accompanies dinner. At a restaurant, patrons are helped to make good food-wine pairings by the restaurant's <a href="/wiki/Sommelier" title="Sommelier">sommelier</a> or wine waiter. Individuals dining at home may use wine guides to help make food‚Äìwine pairings. Wine is also drunk without the accompaniment of a meal in <a href="/wiki/Wine_bar" title="Wine bar">wine bars</a> or with a selection of cheeses (at a wine and cheese party).
</p><p>Wine is important in cuisine not just for its value as a beverage, but as a flavor agent, primarily in <a href="/wiki/Stock_(food)" title="Stock (food)">stocks</a> and <a href="/wiki/Braising" title="Braising">braising</a>, since its acidity lends balance to rich <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Basic_taste#Savouriness" title="Basic taste">savory</a> or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sweet" title="Sweet">sweet</a> dishes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Wine_sauce" title="Wine sauce">Wine sauce</a> is an example of a culinary sauce that uses wine as a primary ingredient.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> Natural wines may exhibit a broad range of alcohol content, from below 9% to above 16% <a href="/wiki/Alcohol_by_volume" title="Alcohol by volume">ABV</a>, with most wines being in the 12.5‚Äì14.5% range.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Fortified_wine" title="Fortified wine">Fortified wines</a> (usually with brandy) may contain 20% alcohol or more.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Religious_significance">Religious significance</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alcohol_and_religion" title="Alcohol and religion">Alcohol and religion</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ancient_religions">Ancient religions</span></h3>
<p>The use of wine in ancient <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Near_Eastern" title="Near Eastern">Near Eastern</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ancient_Egyptian" title="Ancient Egyptian">Ancient Egyptian</a> religious ceremonies was common. <a href="/wiki/Libation" title="Libation">Libations</a> often included wine, and the <a href="/wiki/Dionysian_Mysteries" title="Dionysian Mysteries">religious mysteries</a> of Dionysus used wine as a sacramental <a href="/wiki/Entheogen" title="Entheogen">entheogen</a> to induce a mind-altering state.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Judaism">Judaism</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Kosher_wine" title="Kosher wine">Kosher wine</a></div>
<table class="rquote pullquote floatright" role="presentation" style="border-collapse:collapse; border-style:none; float:right; margin:0.5em 0.75em; width:33%;">
<tbody><tr style="text-align:left; vertical-align:top;">
<td style="color:#b2b7f2; font-size:3.3em; font-family:'Times New Roman',serif; font-weight:bold; padding:4px 2px 2px; width:0.5em; line-height: 1em;">‚Äú
</td>
<td style="padding:0 10px;">Baruch atah Hashem (Ado-nai) Eloheinu melech ha-olam, boray p'ree hagafen ‚Äì Praised be the Lord, our God, King of the universe, Creator of the fruit of the vine.
</td>
<td style="color:#b2b7f2; font-size:3.3em; font-family:'Times New Roman',serif; font-weight:bold; padding:4px 2px 2px; text-align:right; vertical-align:bottom; width:0.5em; line-height: 1em;">‚Äù
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td class="rquotecite" colspan="3" style="padding-top:10px; font-size:smaller; line-height:normal; text-align:right;"><cite>‚Äî¬†The blessing over wine said before consuming the drink.</cite>
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Wine is an integral part of <a href="/wiki/Halakha" title="Halakha">Jewish laws and traditions</a>. The <i><a href="/wiki/Kiddush" title="Kiddush">Kiddush</a></i> is a blessing recited over wine or grape juice to sanctify the <a href="/wiki/Shabbat" title="Shabbat">Shabbat</a>. On Pesach (<a href="/wiki/Passover" title="Passover">Passover</a>) during the Seder, it is a Rabbinic obligation of adults to drink four cups of wine.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> In the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tabernacle_(Judaism)" title="Tabernacle (Judaism)">Tabernacle</a> and in the <a href="/wiki/Temple_in_Jerusalem" title="Temple in Jerusalem">Temple in Jerusalem</a>, the libation of wine was part of the sacrificial service.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> Note that this does not mean that wine is a symbol of blood, a common misconception that contributes to the Christian myth of the <a href="/wiki/Blood_libel" title="Blood libel">blood libel</a>.
"It has been one of history's cruel ironies that the blood libel‚Äîaccusations against Jews using the blood of murdered gentile children for the making of wine and matzot‚Äîbecame the false pretext for numerous <a href="/wiki/Pogrom" title="Pogrom">pogroms</a>. And due to the danger, those who live in a place where blood libels occur are <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Halacha" title="Halacha">halachically</a> exempted from using red wine, lest it be seized as "evidence" against them."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reWineBloodlibel_111-0"><a href="#cite_note-reWineBloodlibel-111">[111]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Christianity">Christianity</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Christian_views_on_alcohol" title="Christian views on alcohol">Christian views on alcohol</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alcohol_in_the_Bible" title="Alcohol in the Bible">Alcohol in the Bible</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_Marriage_at_Cana_-_Decani.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1103" data-file-width="456" height="411" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/The_Marriage_at_Cana_-_Decani.jpg/170px-The_Marriage_at_Cana_-_Decani.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/The_Marriage_at_Cana_-_Decani.jpg/255px-The_Marriage_at_Cana_-_Decani.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/The_Marriage_at_Cana_-_Decani.jpg/340px-The_Marriage_at_Cana_-_Decani.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_Marriage_at_Cana_-_Decani.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Jesus" title="Jesus">Jesus</a> making wine from water in <i><a href="/wiki/Marriage_at_Cana" title="Marriage at Cana">The Marriage at Cana</a></i>, a 14th-century <a href="/wiki/Fresco" title="Fresco">fresco</a> from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Visoki_De%C4%8Dani_monastery" title="Visoki Deƒçani monastery">Visoki Deƒçani monastery</a></div></div></div>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a>, wine is used in a sacred rite called the <a href="/wiki/Eucharist" title="Eucharist">Eucharist</a>, which originates in the <a href="/wiki/Gospel" title="Gospel">Gospel</a> account of the <a href="/wiki/Last_Supper" title="Last Supper">Last Supper</a> (<a href="/wiki/Gospel_of_Luke" title="Gospel of Luke">Gospel of Luke</a> 22:19) describing <a href="/wiki/Jesus" title="Jesus">Jesus</a> sharing bread and wine with his disciples and commanding them to "do this in remembrance of me." Beliefs about the nature of the Eucharist vary among <a href="/wiki/Christian_denomination" title="Christian denomination">denominations</a> (see <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eucharistic_theologies_contrasted" title="Eucharistic theologies contrasted">Eucharistic theologies contrasted</a>).
</p><p>While some Christians consider the use of wine from the grape as essential for the validity of the <a href="/wiki/Sacrament" title="Sacrament">sacrament</a>, many Protestants also allow (or require)  <a href="/wiki/Pasteurization" title="Pasteurization">pasteurized</a> grape juice as a substitute. Wine was used in Eucharistic rites by all Protestant groups until an alternative arose in the late 19th century. <a href="/wiki/Methodism" title="Methodism">Methodist</a> <a href="/wiki/Dentist" title="Dentist">dentist</a> and <a href="/wiki/Prohibition" title="Prohibition">prohibitionist</a> <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Bramwell_Welch" title="Thomas Bramwell Welch">Thomas Bramwell Welch</a> applied new pasteurization techniques to stop the natural fermentation process of <a href="/wiki/Grape_juice" title="Grape juice">grape juice</a>. Some Christians who were part of the growing <a href="/wiki/Temperance_movement" title="Temperance movement">temperance movement</a> pressed for a switch from wine to grape juice, and the substitution spread quickly over much of the United States, as well as to other countries to a lesser degree.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> There remains an ongoing debate between some American <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Protestant" title="Protestant">Protestant</a> denominations as to whether wine can and should be used for the Eucharist or allowed as an ordinary beverage, with Catholics and some mainline Protestants allowing wine drinking in moderation, and some conservative Protestant groups opposing consumption of alcohol altogether.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Islam">Islam</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mei.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="599" data-file-width="448" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Mei.jpg/170px-Mei.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Mei.jpg/255px-Mei.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Mei.jpg/340px-Mei.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mei.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>All alcohol is prohibited under <a href="/wiki/Sharia" title="Sharia">Islamic law</a>, although there has been a long tradition of drinking wine in some Islamic areas, especially in <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a>.</div></div></div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Islam_and_alcohol" title="Islam and alcohol">Islam and alcohol</a></div>
<p>Alcoholic beverages, including wine, are forbidden under most interpretations of <a href="/wiki/Sharia" title="Sharia">Islamic law</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> In many Muslim countries, possession or consumption of alcoholic beverages carry legal penalties. <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a> had previously had <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Viticulture_in_Iran" title="Viticulture in Iran">a thriving wine industry</a> that disappeared after the <a href="/wiki/Iranian_Revolution" title="Iranian Revolution">Islamic Revolution</a> in 1979.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> In <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greater_Persia" title="Greater Persia">Greater Persia</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Persian_wine" title="Persian wine">mey</a></i> (Persian wine) was a central theme of <a href="/wiki/Poetry" title="Poetry">poetry</a> for more than a thousand years, long before the advent of Islam. Some <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alevi" title="Alevi">Alevi</a> sects‚Äìone of the two main branches of Islam in Turkey (the other being <a href="/wiki/Sunni_Islam" title="Sunni Islam">Sunni Islam</a>)‚Äìuse wine in their religious services.
</p><p>Certain exceptions to the ban on alcohol apply. Alcohol derived from a source other than the grape (or its byproducts) and the date<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> is allowed in "very small quantities" (loosely defined as a quantity that does not cause intoxication) under the Sunni <a href="/wiki/Hanafi" title="Hanafi">Hanafi</a> <i>madhab</i>, for specific purposes (such as medicines), where the goal is not intoxication. However, modern Hanafi scholars regard alcohol consumption as totally forbidden.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Health_effects">Health effects</span></h2>

<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Red_wine_headache" title="Red wine headache">Red wine headache</a></div>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Short-term_effects">Short-term effects</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Short-term_effects_of_alcohol" title="Short-term effects of alcohol">Short-term effects of alcohol</a></div>
<p>Wine contains <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ethyl_alcohol" title="Ethyl alcohol">ethyl alcohol</a>, the same chemical that is present in <a href="/wiki/Beer" title="Beer">beer</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Distilled_spirits" title="Distilled spirits">distilled spirits</a> and as such, wine consumption has short-term psychological and physiological effects on the user. Different concentrations of alcohol in the human body have different effects on a person. The effects of alcohol depend on the amount an individual has drunk, the percentage of alcohol in the wine and the timespan that the consumption took place, the amount of food eaten and whether an individual has taken other prescription, over-the-counter or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Street_drugs" title="Street drugs">street drugs</a>, among other factors. Drinking enough to cause a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Blood_alcohol_concentration" title="Blood alcohol concentration">blood alcohol concentration</a> (BAC) of 0.03%-0.12% typically causes an overall improvement in mood and possible <a href="/wiki/Euphoria" title="Euphoria">euphoria</a>, increased self-confidence and sociability, decreased anxiety, a <a href="/wiki/Alcohol_flush_reaction" title="Alcohol flush reaction">flushed, red appearance in the face</a> and impaired judgment and fine muscle coordination. A BAC of 0.09% to 0.25% causes <a href="/wiki/Lethargy" title="Lethargy">lethargy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sedation" title="Sedation">sedation</a>, balance problems and blurred vision. A BAC from 0.18% to 0.30% causes profound confusion, impaired speech (e.g. slurred speech), staggering, dizziness and vomiting. A BAC from 0.25% to 0.40% causes <a href="/wiki/Stupor" title="Stupor">stupor</a>, unconsciousness, <a href="/wiki/Anterograde_amnesia" title="Anterograde amnesia">anterograde amnesia</a>, vomiting, and death may occur due to inhalation of vomit (<a href="/wiki/Pulmonary_aspiration" title="Pulmonary aspiration">pulmonary aspiration</a>) while unconscious and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Respiratory_depression" title="Respiratory depression">respiratory depression</a> (potentially life-threatening). A BAC from 0.35% to 0.80% causes a <a href="/wiki/Coma" title="Coma">coma</a> (unconsciousness), life-threatening respiratory depression and possibly fatal <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alcohol_poisoning" title="Alcohol poisoning">alcohol poisoning</a>. As with all alcoholic beverages, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Drinking_and_driving" title="Drinking and driving">drinking while driving</a>, operating an aircraft or heavy machinery increases the risk of an accident; many countries have penalties against drunk driving.
</p><p>Wines can trigger the positive emotions in a short period of time, such as relaxed and comfortable. The context and quality of wine can affect the mood and emotions, too. <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Long-term_effects">Long-term effects</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Long-term_effects_of_alcohol_consumption" title="Long-term effects of alcohol consumption">Long-term effects of alcohol consumption</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Possible_long-term_effects_of_ethanol.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1485" data-file-width="2079" height="157" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Possible_long-term_effects_of_ethanol.svg/220px-Possible_long-term_effects_of_ethanol.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Possible_long-term_effects_of_ethanol.svg/330px-Possible_long-term_effects_of_ethanol.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Possible_long-term_effects_of_ethanol.svg/440px-Possible_long-term_effects_of_ethanol.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Possible_long-term_effects_of_ethanol.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Most significant of the possible <a href="/wiki/Long-term_effects_of_alcohol_consumption" title="Long-term effects of alcohol consumption">long-term effects</a> of <a href="/wiki/Ethanol" title="Ethanol">ethanol</a>, one of the constituents of wine. Consumption of alcohol by pregnant mothers may result in <a href="/wiki/Fetal_alcohol_spectrum_disorder" title="Fetal alcohol spectrum disorder">fetal alcohol spectrum disorders</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>The main active ingredient of wine is alcohol, and therefore, the health effects of alcohol apply to wine. A 2016 systematic review and meta-analysis found that moderate ethanol consumption brought no mortality benefit compared with lifetime abstention from ethanol consumption.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup> A systematic analysis of data from the Global Burden of Disease study found that consumption of ethanol increases the risk of cancer and increases the risk of all-cause mortality, and that the level of ethanol consumption that minimizes disease is zero consumption. <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> Some studies have concluded that drinking small quantities of alcohol (less than one drink in women and two in men) is associated with a <i>decreased</i> risk of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Heart_disease" title="Heart disease">heart disease</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stroke" title="Stroke">stroke</a>, <a href="/wiki/Diabetes_mellitus" title="Diabetes mellitus">diabetes mellitus</a>, and early death.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kee2014_120-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kee2014-120">[120]</a></sup> Some of these studies lumped former ethanol drinkers and life-long abstainers into a single group of nondrinkers, hiding the health benefits of life-long abstention from ethanol.  Drinking more than this amount actually increases the risk of heart disease, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/High_blood_pressure" title="High blood pressure">high blood pressure</a>, <a href="/wiki/Atrial_fibrillation" title="Atrial fibrillation">atrial fibrillation</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Stroke" title="Stroke">stroke</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kee2014_120-1"><a href="#cite_note-Kee2014-120">[120]</a></sup> Risk is greater in younger people due to <a href="/wiki/Binge_drinking" title="Binge drinking">binge drinking</a> which may result in violence or accidents.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kee2014_120-2"><a href="#cite_note-Kee2014-120">[120]</a></sup> About 3.3 million deaths (5.9% of all deaths) are believed to be due to alcohol each year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NIH2015Stats_121-0"><a href="#cite_note-NIH2015Stats-121">[121]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Alcoholism" title="Alcoholism">Alcoholism</a> is a broad term for any drinking of <a href="/wiki/Ethanol" title="Ethanol">alcohol</a> that results in problems.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> It was previously divided into two types: <a href="/wiki/Alcohol_abuse" title="Alcohol abuse">alcohol abuse</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alcohol_dependence" title="Alcohol dependence">alcohol dependence</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NIH2003_123-0"><a href="#cite_note-NIH2003-123">[123]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NIH2013_124-0"><a href="#cite_note-NIH2013-124">[124]</a></sup> In a medical context, alcoholism is said to exist when two or more of the following conditions is present: a person drinks large amounts over a long time period, has difficulty cutting down, acquiring and drinking alcohol takes up a great deal of time, alcohol is strongly desired, usage results in not fulfilling responsibilities, usage results in social problems, usage results in health problems, usage results in risky situations, <a href="/wiki/Alcohol_withdrawal_syndrome" title="Alcohol withdrawal syndrome">withdrawal</a> occurs when stopping, and <a href="/wiki/Alcohol_tolerance" title="Alcohol tolerance">alcohol tolerance</a> has occurred with use.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NIH2013_124-1"><a href="#cite_note-NIH2013-124">[124]</a></sup> Alcoholism reduces a person's life expectancy by around ten years<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Schu2014_125-0"><a href="#cite_note-Schu2014-125">[125]</a></sup> and alcohol use is the third leading cause of early death in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kee2014_120-3"><a href="#cite_note-Kee2014-120">[120]</a></sup> No professional medical association recommends that people who are nondrinkers should start drinking wine.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kee2014_120-4"><a href="#cite_note-Kee2014-120">[120]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup>
</p><p>Excessive consumption of alcohol can cause <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Liver_cirrhosis" title="Liver cirrhosis">liver cirrhosis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alcoholism" title="Alcoholism">alcoholism</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/American_Heart_Association" title="American Heart Association">American Heart Association</a> "cautions people NOT to start drinking ... if they do not already drink alcohol. Consult your doctor on the benefits and risks of consuming alcohol in moderation."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup>
</p><p>Population studies exhibit a <a href="/wiki/J_curve" title="J curve">J-curve</a> correlation between wine consumption and rates of heart disease: heavy drinkers have an elevated rate, while people who drink small amount (up to 20¬†g of alcohol per day, approximately 200¬†ml (7¬†imp¬†fl¬†oz; 7¬†US¬†fl¬†oz) of 12.7% <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ABV" title="ABV">ABV</a> wine) have a lower rate than non-drinkers. Studies have also found that moderate consumption of other alcoholic beverages is correlated with decreased mortality from cardiovascular causes,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup> although the association is stronger for wine. Additionally, some studies have found a greater correlation of health benefits with red than white wine, though other studies have found no difference. Red wine contains more <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Polyphenols_in_wine" title="Polyphenols in wine">polyphenols</a> than white wine, and these could be protective against cardiovascular disease.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lindberg_130-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lindberg-130">[130]</a></sup>
</p><p>Although red wine contains the chemical <a href="/wiki/Resveratrol" title="Resveratrol">resveratrol</a> and there is tentative evidence it may improve heart health, the evidence is unclear for those at high risk as of  2013<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Wine&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup> Grape skins naturally produce resveratrol in response to fungal infection, including exposure to yeast during <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fermentation_(wine)" title="Fermentation (wine)">fermentation</a>. White wine generally contains lower levels of the chemical as it has minimal contact with grape skins during this process.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Forgery_and_manipulation">Forgery and manipulation</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Brooklyn_Museum_-_All_These_Grapes_Seem_to_Have_Fallen_Ill..._(Tous_ces_raisins_me_font_l%27effet_d%27avoir_la_maladie...)_-_Honor%C3%A9_Daumier.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="613" data-file-width="768" height="160" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Brooklyn_Museum_-_All_These_Grapes_Seem_to_Have_Fallen_Ill..._%28Tous_ces_raisins_me_font_l%27effet_d%27avoir_la_maladie...%29_-_Honor%C3%A9_Daumier.jpg/200px-Brooklyn_Museum_-_All_These_Grapes_Seem_to_Have_Fallen_Ill..._%28Tous_ces_raisins_me_font_l%27effet_d%27avoir_la_maladie...%29_-_Honor%C3%A9_Daumier.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Brooklyn_Museum_-_All_These_Grapes_Seem_to_Have_Fallen_Ill..._%28Tous_ces_raisins_me_font_l%27effet_d%27avoir_la_maladie...%29_-_Honor%C3%A9_Daumier.jpg/300px-Brooklyn_Museum_-_All_These_Grapes_Seem_to_Have_Fallen_Ill..._%28Tous_ces_raisins_me_font_l%27effet_d%27avoir_la_maladie...%29_-_Honor%C3%A9_Daumier.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Brooklyn_Museum_-_All_These_Grapes_Seem_to_Have_Fallen_Ill..._%28Tous_ces_raisins_me_font_l%27effet_d%27avoir_la_maladie...%29_-_Honor%C3%A9_Daumier.jpg/400px-Brooklyn_Museum_-_All_These_Grapes_Seem_to_Have_Fallen_Ill..._%28Tous_ces_raisins_me_font_l%27effet_d%27avoir_la_maladie...%29_-_Honor%C3%A9_Daumier.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Brooklyn_Museum_-_All_These_Grapes_Seem_to_Have_Fallen_Ill..._(Tous_ces_raisins_me_font_l%27effet_d%27avoir_la_maladie...)_-_Honor%C3%A9_Daumier.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Honor%C3%A9_Daumier" title="Honor√© Daumier">Honor√© Daumier</a>: <i>All These Grapes Seem to Have Fallen Ill...</i> (<i>Tous ces raisins me font l'effet d'avoir la maladie...</i>)</div></div></div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Wine_fraud" title="Wine fraud">Wine fraud</a></div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_food_contamination_incidents" title="List of food contamination incidents">List of food contamination incidents</a></div>
<p>Incidents of fraud, such as mislabeling the origin or quality of wines, have resulted in regulations on labeling. "Wine scandals" that have received media attention include:
</p>
<ul><li>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1985_Diethylene_Glycol_Wine_Scandal" title="1985 Diethylene Glycol Wine Scandal">1985 Diethylene Glycol Wine Scandal</a>, in which <a href="/wiki/Diethylene_glycol" title="Diethylene glycol">diethylene glycol</a> was used as a sweetener in some Austrian wines.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Wine_fraud#Hazardous_materials" title="Wine fraud">In 1986</a>, <a href="/wiki/Methanol" title="Methanol">methanol</a> (a toxic type of alcohol) was used to alter certain wines manufactured in <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a>.</li>
<li>In 2008, some Italian wines were found to include <a href="/wiki/Sulfuric_acid" title="Sulfuric acid">sulfuric acid</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hydrochloric_acid" title="Hydrochloric acid">hydrochloric acid</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup></li>
<li>In 2010, some Chinese red wines were found to be adulterated, and as a consequence China's Hebei province has shut down nearly 30 wineries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Packaging">Packaging</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Cork_(material)" title="Cork (material)">Cork (material)</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Closure_(bottle)" title="Closure (bottle)">Closure (bottle)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alternative_wine_closure" title="Alternative wine closure">Alternative wine closure</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wine_bottle" title="Wine bottle">Wine bottle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Box_wine" title="Box wine">Box wine</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Screw_cap_(wine)" title="Screw cap (wine)">Screw cap (wine)</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Corks019.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1232" data-file-width="1632" height="128" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Corks019.jpg/170px-Corks019.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Corks019.jpg/255px-Corks019.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Corks019.jpg/340px-Corks019.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Corks019.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Assorted <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wine_cork" title="Wine cork">wine corks</a></div></div></div>
<p>Most wines are sold in <a href="/wiki/Wine_bottle" title="Wine bottle">glass bottles</a> and sealed with <a href="/wiki/Cork_(material)" title="Cork (material)">corks</a> (50% of which come from <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup> An increasing number of wine producers have been using <a href="/wiki/Alternative_wine_closure" title="Alternative wine closure">alternative closures</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Screw_cap_(wine)" title="Screw cap (wine)">screwcaps</a> and synthetic <a href="/wiki/Plastic" title="Plastic">plastic</a> "corks". Although alternative closures are less expensive and prevent <a href="/wiki/Cork_taint" title="Cork taint">cork taint</a>, they have been blamed for such problems as excessive <a href="/wiki/Redox" title="Redox">reduction</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup>
</p><p>Some wines are packaged in thick plastic bags within <a href="/wiki/Corrugated_fiberboard" title="Corrugated fiberboard">corrugated fiberboard</a> boxes, and are called "<a href="/wiki/Box_wine" title="Box wine">box wines</a>", or "cask wine". Tucked inside the package is a tap affixed to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bag_in_box" title="Bag in box">bag in box</a>, or bladder, that is later extended by the consumer for serving the contents. Box wine can stay acceptably fresh for up to a month after opening because the bladder collapses as wine is dispensed, limiting contact with air and, thus, slowing the rate of oxidation. In contrast, bottled wine <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oxidize" title="Oxidize">oxidizes</a> more rapidly after opening because of the increasing ratio of air to wine as the contents are dispensed; it can degrade considerably in a few days.
</p><p>Environmental considerations of wine packaging reveal benefits and drawbacks of both bottled and box wines. The glass used to make bottles is a nontoxic, naturally occurring substance that is completely recyclable, whereas the plastics used for box-wine containers are typically much less environmentally friendly. However, wine-bottle manufacturers have been cited for <a href="/wiki/Clean_Air_Act_(United_States)" title="Clean Air Act (United States)">Clean Air Act</a> violations. A <i>New York Times</i> editorial suggested that box wine, being lighter in package weight, has a reduced <a href="/wiki/Carbon_footprint" title="Carbon footprint">carbon footprint</a> from its distribution; however, box-wine plastics, even though possibly recyclable, can be more labor-intensive (and therefore expensive) to process than glass bottles. In addition, while a wine box is recyclable, its plastic bladder most likely is not.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup>
</p><p>Some wine is sold in <a href="/wiki/Stainless_steel" title="Stainless steel">stainless steel</a> kegs and is referred to as <a href="/wiki/Wine_on_tap" title="Wine on tap">wine on tap</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Storage">Storage</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Storage_of_wine" title="Storage of wine">Storage of wine</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wine_Barrels.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2336" data-file-width="3183" height="125" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Wine_Barrels.jpg/170px-Wine_Barrels.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Wine_Barrels.jpg/255px-Wine_Barrels.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Wine_Barrels.jpg/340px-Wine_Barrels.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Wine_Barrels.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Oak" title="Oak">Oak</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wine_barrel" title="Wine barrel">wine barrels</a></div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Wine_cellar" title="Wine cellar">Wine cellars</a>, or wine rooms, if they are above-ground, are places designed specifically for the storage and aging of wine. Fine restaurants and some private homes have wine cellars. In an active wine cellar, temperature and humidity are maintained by a climate-control system. Passive wine cellars are not climate-controlled, and so must be carefully located. Because wine is a natural, perishable food product, all types‚Äîincluding red, white, sparkling, and fortified‚Äîcan spoil when exposed to heat, light, vibration or fluctuations in temperature and humidity. When properly stored, wines can maintain their quality and in some cases improve in aroma, flavor, and complexity as they age. Some wine experts contend that the optimal temperature for aging wine is 13¬†¬∞C (55¬†¬∞F),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup> others 15¬†¬∞C (59¬†¬∞F).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup>
</p><p>Wine refrigerators offer a smaller alternative to wine cellars and are available in capacities ranging from small, 16-bottle units to furniture-quality pieces that can contain 400 bottles. Wine refrigerators are not ideal for aging, but rather serve to chill wine to the proper temperature for drinking. These refrigerators keep the humidity low (usually under 50%), below the optimal humidity of 50% to 70%. Lower humidity levels can dry out corks over time, allowing oxygen to enter the bottle, which reduces the wine's quality through oxidation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup> While some types of alcohol are sometimes stored in freezer, such as <a href="/wiki/Vodka" title="Vodka">vodka</a>, it is not possible to safely freeze wine in the bottle, as there is insufficient room for it to expand as it freezes and the bottle will usually crack. Certain shapes of bottle may allow the cork to be pushed out by the ice, but if the bottle is frozen on its side, the wine in the narrower neck will invariably freeze first, preventing this.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Professions">Professions</span></h2>
<p>There are a large number of occupations and professions that are part of the wine industry, ranging from the individuals who grow the grapes, prepare the wine, bottle it, sell it, assess it, market it and finally make recommendations to clients and serve the wine.
</p>
<table class="wikitable">
<caption>Related professions
</caption>
<tbody><tr>
<th>Name
</th>
<th>Description
</th></tr>
<tr>
<td>Cellar master
</td>
<td>A person in charge of a wine cellar
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><a href="/wiki/Cooper_(profession)" title="Cooper (profession)">Cooper</a>
</td>
<td>A craftsperson of wooden barrels and casks. A <a href="/wiki/Cooper_(profession)" title="Cooper (profession)">cooperage</a> is a facility that produces such casks
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/N%C3%A9gociant" title="N√©gociant">N√©gociant</a>
</td>
<td>A wine merchant who purchases the product of smaller growers or wine-makers to sell them under its own name
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oenologist" title="Oenologist">Oenologist</a>
</td>
<td>A wine scientist or <a href="/wiki/Wine_chemistry" title="Wine chemistry">wine chemist</a>; a student of <a href="/wiki/Oenology" title="Oenology">oenology</a>. In the 2000s, B.Sc. degrees in oenology and <a href="/wiki/Viticulture" title="Viticulture">viticulture</a> are available. A wine-maker may be trained as an oenologist, but often hires one as a consultant
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><a href="/wiki/Sommelier" title="Sommelier">Sommelier</a>
</td>
<td>Also called a "wine steward", this is a specialist wine expert in charge of developing a restaurant's <a href="/wiki/Wine_list" title="Wine list">wine list</a>, educating the staff about wine, and assisting customers with their selections (especially food‚Äìwine pairings)
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vintner" title="Vintner">Vintner</a>, <a href="/wiki/Winemaker" title="Winemaker">Winemaker</a>
</td>
<td>A wine producer; a person who makes wine
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Viticulturist" title="Viticulturist">Viticulturist</a>
</td>
<td>A specialist in the science of grapevines; a manager of vineyard pruning, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Irrigation_(wine)" title="Irrigation (wine)">irrigation</a>, and pest control
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><a href="/wiki/Wine_critic" title="Wine critic">Wine critic</a>
</td>
<td>A wine expert and journalist who tastes and reviews wines for books and magazines
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wine_taster" title="Wine taster">Wine taster</a>
</td>
<td>A wine expert who tastes wines to ascertain their quality and flavour
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>Wine waiter
</td>
<td>A restaurant or <a href="/wiki/Wine_bar" title="Wine bar">wine bar</a> <a href="/wiki/Waiting_staff" title="Waiting staff">server</a> with a basic- to mid-level knowledge of wine and food‚Äìwine pairings
</td></tr></tbody></table>
